<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top:#aaa 1px solid"><a href="/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_symbols" title="Lists of United States state symbols">Lists of United States state symbols</a></td>

<p><b>New York</b> is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern United States</a>. New York was one of the original <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">thirteen colonies</a> that formed the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. With an estimated 19.8 million residents in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-9">[9]</a></sup> it is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population" title="List of U.S. states by population">fourth most populous state</a> in the United States. To differentiate from its city with the same name, it is sometimes called <b>New York State</b>.</p>
<p>The state's largest city, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, makes up over 40% of the state's population. Two-thirds of the state's population lives in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a>, and nearly 40% lives on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCest2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCest2-10">[10]</a></sup> The state and city were both named for the 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_York" title="Duke of York">Duke of York</a>, future <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">King James II of England</a>. With an estimated population of 8.55 million in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCest2_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYCest2-10">[10]</a></sup> New York City is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">most populous city</a> in the United States and the premier gateway for legal <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigration to the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigrants2014est_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Immigrants2014est-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigrants2013est_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Immigrants2013est-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigrants2012est_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Immigrants2012est-13">[13]</a></sup> The New York Metropolitan Area is one of the most populous <a href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">urban agglomerations</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> New York City is a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Headquarters" title="United Nations Headquarters">United Nations Headquarters</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and has been described as the cultural, financial, and <a href="/wiki/Media_(communication)" title="Media (communication)">media</a> capital<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> of the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-culture1_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-culture1-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-culture2_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-culture2-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-culture3_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-culture3-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-culture4_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-culture4-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter-24">[24]</a></sup> as well as the world's most economically powerful city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomicallyPowerful2015_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-EconomicallyPowerful2015-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The next four most populous cities in the state are <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_capitals" title="List of U.S. state capitals">state capital</a> is <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>.</p>
<p>New York has a diverse geography. The state is bordered by <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> to the south and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> to the east. The state has a <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime border</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> with <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, east of Long Island, as well as an <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">international border</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_provinces" title="Canadian provinces">Canadian provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> to the northwest. The southern part of the state consists of Long Island and several smaller associated islands, as well as New York City and the lower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hudson_River_Valley" title="Hudson River Valley">Hudson River Valley</a>, most of which lie within the wider <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coastal_Plain" title="Atlantic Coastal Plain">Atlantic Coastal Plain</a>. The large region known as <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a> consists of several ranges of the wider <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">Allegheny Plateau</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catskills" title="Catskills">Catskills</a> along New York's <a href="/wiki/Southern_Tier" title="Southern Tier">Southern Tier</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_Mountains" title="Adirondack Mountains">Adirondack Mountains</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Country_(New_York)" title="North Country (New York)">Northeastern lobe</a> of the state. These more mountainous regions are bisected by two major river valleys—the north-south Hudson River Valley and the east-west <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk River</a> Valley, which forms the core of the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a>. <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">Western New York</a> is considered part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Region" title="Great Lakes Region">Great Lakes Region</a> and straddles <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>. Between the two lakes lies <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">Niagara Falls</a>. The central part of the state is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Finger_Lakes" title="Finger Lakes">Finger Lakes</a>, a popular vacation and tourist destination.</p>
<p>New York had been inhabited by tribes of <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">Algonquian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iroquoian_languages" title="Iroquoian languages">Iroquoian</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> for several hundred years by the time the earliest Europeans came to New York. <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French colonists</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit_missionaries" title="Jesuit missionaries">Jesuit missionaries</a> arrived southward from <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> for trade and proselytizing. In 1609, the region was visited by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">Henry Hudson</a> sailing for the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> built <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nassau_(North_River)" title="Fort Nassau (North River)">Fort Nassau</a> in 1614 at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk</a> rivers, where the present-day capital of Albany later developed. The Dutch soon also settled <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> and parts of the Hudson Valley, establishing the multicultural colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>, a center of trade and immigration. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> seized the colony from the Dutch in 1664. During the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> (1775–1783), a group of colonists of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">Province of New York</a> attempted to take control of the British colony and eventually succeeded in establishing independence.</p>
<p>Many landmarks in New York are well known, including four of the world's ten most-visited tourist attractions in 2013: <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>, Niagara Falls (shared with <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">Grand Central Terminal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ann_Shields_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ann_Shields-27">[27]</a></sup> New York is home to the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>, a symbol of the United States and its ideals of freedom, <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, and opportunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In the 21st century, New York has emerged as a global node of <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">creativity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurship</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalNY1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-29">[29]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_tolerance" title="Social tolerance">social tolerance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SocialToleranceNY1_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-SocialToleranceNY1-30">[30]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">environmental sustainability</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY1-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY2_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY2-32">[32]</a></sup> New York's <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_New_York" title="List of colleges and universities in New York">higher education network</a> comprises approximately 200 colleges and universities, including <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">Rockefeller University</a>, which have been ranked among the top 35 in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_York_(state)" title="History of New York (state)">History of New York (state)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_American_history">Native American history</span></h3>
<p>The tribes in what is now New York were predominantly Iroquois and Algonquin. <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> was divided roughly in half between the <a href="/wiki/Wampanoag" title="Wampanoag">Wampanoag</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Lenape</a>. The Lenape also controlled most of the region surrounding <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a>. North of the Lenape was a third Algonquin nation, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohicans" title="Mohicans">Mohicans</a>. Starting north of them, from east to west, were three Iroquoian nations: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohawk_nation" title="Mohawk nation">Mohawk</a>, the original <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Petun" title="Petun">Petun</a>. South of them, divided roughly along <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">Appalachia</a>, were the <a href="/wiki/Susquehannock" title="Susquehannock">Susquehannock</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erie_(tribe)" title="Erie (tribe)">Erie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the Wampanoag and Mohican peoples were caught up in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Phillip%27s_War" title="King Phillip's War">King Phillip's War</a>, a joint effort of many <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> tribes to push Europeans off their land. After the death of their leader, Chief Phillip <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Metcomet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Metcomet (page does not exist)">Metcomet</a>, most of those peoples fled inland, splitting into the <a href="/wiki/Abenaki" title="Abenaki">Abenaki</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schaghticoke_people" title="Schaghticoke people">Schaghticoke</a>. Many of the Mohicans remained in the region until the 1800s, however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mohawk and Susquehannock were the most militaristic. Trying to corner trade with the Europeans, they targeted other tribes. The Mohawk were also known for refusing white settlement on their land and banishing any of their people who converted to Christianity. They posed a major threat to the Abenaki and Mohicans, while the Susquehannock briefly conquered the Lenape in the 1600s. The most devastating event of the century, however, was the <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Wars" title="Beaver Wars">Beaver Wars</a>. From approximately 1640–1680, Iroquoian peoples waged campaigns which extended from modern day Michigan to Virginia against Algonquin and Siouan tribes, as well as each other. The aim was to control more land for animal trapping, a career most natives had turned to in hopes of trading with whites first. Not only did this completely change the ethnography of the region, most large game was hunted out before whites ever fully explored the land. Still, afterward, the Iroquois Confederacy offered shelter to refugees of the <a href="/wiki/Mascouten" title="Mascouten">Mascouten</a>, Erie, <a href="/wiki/Neutral_Nation" title="Neutral Nation">Chonnonton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tutelo" title="Tutelo">Tutelo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saponi" title="Saponi">Saponi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuscarora_people" title="Tuscarora people">Tuscarora</a> nations. In the 1700s, they would also merge with the Mohawk during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French-Indian_War" title="French-Indian War">French-Indian War</a> and take in the remaining Susquehannock of Pennsylvania after they were decimated in war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Most of these other groups blended in until they ceased to exist. Then, after the Revolution, a large group of them split off and returned to Ohio, becoming known as the <a href="/wiki/Mingo" title="Mingo">Mingo</a> Seneca. The current six tribes of the Iroquois Confederacy are the Seneca, Cayuga, Onondaga, Oneida, Tuscarora and Mohawk. As the Iroquois sided with the British during the Revolution, they soon after migrated to Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the Lenape formed a close relationship with <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">William Penn</a>. However, upon Penn's death, his sons managed to take over much of their lands and banish them to Ohio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> When the U.S. drafted the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Removal_Act" title="Indian Removal Act">Indian Removal Act</a>, the Lenape were further moved to Missouri, whereas their cousins, the Mohicans, were sent to Wisconsin.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_century">16th century</span></h3>
<p>In 1524, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a>, an Italian explorer in the service of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_crown" title="French crown">French crown</a>, explored the Atlantic coast of North America between the Carolinas and Newfoundland, including <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Narragansett_Bay" title="Narragansett Bay">Narragansett Bay</a>. On April 17, 1524 Verrazanno entered <a href="/wiki/New_York_Bay" title="New York Bay">New York Bay</a>, by way of the strait now called <a href="/wiki/The_Narrows" title="The Narrows">the Narrows</a> into the northern bay which he named Santa Margherita, in honor of the King of France's <a href="/wiki/Marguerite_de_Navarre" title="Marguerite de Navarre">sister</a>. Verrazzano described it as "a vast coastline with a deep delta in which every kind of ship could pass" and he adds: "that it extends inland for a league and opens up to form a beautiful lake. This vast sheet of water swarmed with native boats". He landed on the tip of Manhattan and possibly on the furthest point of Long Island. Verrazanno's stay was interrupted by a storm which pushed him north towards <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">Martha's Vineyard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1540 French traders from New France built a chateau on <a href="/wiki/Castle_Island_(New_York)" title="Castle Island (New York)">Castle Island</a>, within present-day Albany; due to flooding, it was abandoned the next year. In 1614, the Dutch under the command of Hendrick Corstiaensen, rebuilt the French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chateau" title="Chateau">chateau</a>, which they called <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nassau_(North_River)" title="Fort Nassau (North River)">Fort Nassau</a>. Fort Nassau was the first Dutch settlement in North America, and was located along the Hudson River, also within present-day Albany. The small fort served as a trading post and warehouse. Located on the Hudson River flood plain, the rudimentary "fort" was washed away by flooding in 1617,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and abandoned for good after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Orange" title="Fort Orange">Fort Orange (New Netherland)</a> was built nearby in 1623.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicles_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicles-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">17th century</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">Province of New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castelloplan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2401" data-file-width="3267" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Castelloplan.jpg/220px-Castelloplan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Castelloplan.jpg/330px-Castelloplan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Castelloplan.jpg/440px-Castelloplan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castelloplan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a>, present-day Lower Manhattan, 1660</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Henry Hudson's 1609 voyage marked the beginning of European involvement with the area. Sailing for the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> and looking for a passage to Asia, he entered the <a href="/wiki/Upper_New_York_Bay" title="Upper New York Bay">Upper New York Bay</a> on September 11 of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Word of his findings encouraged Dutch merchants to explore the coast in search for profitable fur trading with local Native American tribes.</p>
<p>During the 17th century, Dutch <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> established for the trade of pelts from the <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Lenape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a>, and other tribes were founded in the colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a>. The first of these trading posts were <a href="/wiki/Fort_Nassau_(North_River)" title="Fort Nassau (North River)">Fort Nassau</a> (1614, near present-day <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>); <a href="/wiki/Fort_Orange_(New_Netherland)" title="Fort Orange (New Netherland)">Fort Orange</a> (1624, on the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> just south of the current city of Albany and created to replace Fort Nassau), developing into settlement <a href="/wiki/Beverwijck" title="Beverwijck">Beverwijck</a> (1647), and into what became Albany; <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam" title="Fort Amsterdam">Fort Amsterdam</a> (1625, to develop into the town <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> which is present-day New York City); and Esopus, (1653, now <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_New_York" title="Kingston, New York">Kingston</a>). The success of the <a href="/wiki/Patroon" title="Patroon">patroonship</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manor_of_Rensselaerswyck" title="Manor of Rensselaerswyck">Rensselaerswyck</a> (1630), which surrounded Albany and lasted until the mid-19th century, was also a key factor in the early success of the colony. The English captured the colony during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a> and governed it as the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">Province of New York</a>. The city of New York was recaptured by the Dutch in 1673 during the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Third Anglo-Dutch War">Third Anglo-Dutch War</a> (1672–1674) and renamed New Orange. It was returned to the English under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Westminster_(1674)" title="Treaty of Westminster (1674)">Treaty of Westminster</a> a year later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="18th_century,_the_American_Revolution,_and_statehood"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century.2C_the_American_Revolution.2C_and_statehood">18th century, the American Revolution, and statehood</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3927" data-file-width="3000" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png/170px-NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png/255px-NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png/340px-NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NewYork1777MapRestoredSmall.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New York and neighboring jurisdictions in 1777</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Liberty" title="Sons of Liberty">Sons of Liberty</a> were organized in New York City during the 1760s, largely in response to the oppressive <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_1765" title="Stamp Act 1765">Stamp Act</a> passed by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">British Parliament</a> in 1765. The <a href="/wiki/Stamp_Act_Congress" title="Stamp Act Congress">Stamp Act Congress</a> met in the city on October 19 of that year, composed of representatives from across the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> who set the stage for the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> to follow. The Stamp Act Congress resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Rights_and_Grievances" title="Declaration of Rights and Grievances">Declaration of Rights and Grievances</a>, which was the first written expression by representatives of the Americans of many of the rights and complaints later expressed in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>. This included the right to <a href="/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation" title="No taxation without representation">representative government</a>. At the same time, given strong trading between <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a> and the United States on both business and personal levels, many New York residents were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loyalist" title="Loyalist">Loyalists</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Fort_Ticonderoga" title="Capture of Fort Ticonderoga">Capture of Fort Ticonderoga</a> provided the <a href="/wiki/Fortification_of_Dorchester_Heights" title="Fortification of Dorchester Heights">cannon and gunpowder</a> necessary to force a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> withdrawal from the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Boston" title="Siege of Boston">Siege of Boston</a> in 1775.</p>
<p>New York was the only colony to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence#Draft_and_adoption" title="United States Declaration of Independence">not vote for independence</a>, as the delegates were not authorized to do so. New York then endorsed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> on July 9, 1776.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Constitution" title="New York Constitution">New York State Constitution</a> was framed by a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_meeting)" title="Constitutional convention (political meeting)">convention</a> which assembled at <a href="/wiki/White_Plains,_New_York" title="White Plains, New York">White Plains</a> on July 10, 1776, and after repeated adjournments and changes of location, terminated its labors at <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_New_York" title="Kingston, New York">Kingston</a> on Sunday evening, April 20, 1777, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_New_York,_1777" title="Constitution of New York, 1777">new constitution</a> drafted by <a href="/wiki/John_Jay" title="John Jay">John Jay</a> was adopted with but one dissenting vote. It was not submitted to the people for ratification. On July 30, 1777, <a href="/wiki/George_Clinton_(vice_president)" title="George Clinton (vice president)">George Clinton</a> was inaugurated as the first <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a> at Kingston.</p>
<p>About one-third of the battles of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a> took place in New York; the first major battle after U.S. independence was declared—and the largest battle of the entire war—was fought in New York at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Long_Island" title="Battle of Long Island">Battle of Long Island</a> (a.k.a. <i>Battle of Brooklyn</i>) in August 1776. After their victory, the British occupied New York City, making it their military and political base of operations in North America for the duration of the conflict, and consequently the focus of General <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_operations_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="Intelligence operations in the American Revolutionary War">intelligence network</a>. On the notorious British <a href="/wiki/HMS_Jersey_(1736)" title="HMS Jersey (1736)">prison ships</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wallabout_Bay" title="Wallabout Bay">Wallabout Bay</a>, more American combatants died of intentional neglect than were killed in combat in every battle of the war, combined. Both sides of combatants lost more soldiers to disease than to outright wounds. The first of two major British armies were captured by the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Saratoga" title="Battles of Saratoga">Battle of Saratoga</a> in 1777, a success that influenced <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to ally with the revolutionaries.The state constitution was enacted in 1777. New York became the 11th state to ratify the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, on July 26, 1788.</p>
<table class="wikitable succession-box" style="margin:0.5em auto; font-size:95%;clear:both;">
<tr style="text-align:center;">
<td rowspan="1" style="width:30%;">Preceded by<br/>
<span style="font-weight: bold"><a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a></span></td>
<td rowspan="1" style="width: 40%; text-align: center;"><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_statehood" title="List of U.S. states by date of statehood">List of U.S. states by date of statehood</a></b><br/>
Ratified <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a> on July 26, 1788 (11th)</td>

</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1987" data-file-width="3000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg/220px-Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg/330px-Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg/440px-Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surrender_of_General_Burgoyne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
British general <a href="/wiki/John_Burgoyne" title="John Burgoyne">John Burgoyne</a> surrenders at <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_campaign" title="Saratoga campaign">Saratoga</a> in 1777.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In an attempt to retain their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_nation" title="Sovereign nation">sovereignty</a> and remain an independent nation positioned between the new United States and British North America, four of the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois Nations</a> fought on the side of the British; only the <a href="/wiki/Oneida_people" title="Oneida people">Oneida</a> and their dependents, the Tuscarora, allied themselves with the Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In retaliation for attacks on the frontier led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Brant" title="Joseph Brant">Joseph Brant</a> and Loyalist <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_people" title="Mohawk people">Mohawk forces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sullivan_Expedition" title="Sullivan Expedition">Sullivan Expedition</a> of 1779 destroyed nearly 50 Iroquois villages, adjacent croplands and winter stores, forcing many refugees to British-held Niagara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>As allies of the British, the Iroquois were forced out of New York, although they had not been part of treaty negotiations. They resettled in Canada after the war and were given land grants by the Crown. In the treaty settlement, the British ceded most Indian lands to the new United States. Because New York made treaty with the Iroquois without getting Congressional approval, some of the land purchases have been subject to land claim suits since the late 20th century by the federally recognized tribes. New York put up more than 5 million acres (20,000 km<sup>2</sup>) of former Iroquois territory for sale in the years after the Revolutionary War, leading to rapid development in upstate New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> As per the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a>, the last vestige of British authority in the former <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a>—their troops in New York City—departed in 1783, which was long afterward celebrated as <a href="/wiki/Evacuation_Day_(New_York)" title="Evacuation Day (New York)">Evacuation Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1800LowsNYstate.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2318" data-file-width="2639" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/1800LowsNYstate.jpeg/220px-1800LowsNYstate.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/1800LowsNYstate.jpeg/330px-1800LowsNYstate.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/1800LowsNYstate.jpeg/440px-1800LowsNYstate.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1800LowsNYstate.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1800 map of New York from <a href="/wiki/Low%27s_Encyclopaedia" title="Low's Encyclopaedia">Low's Encyclopaedia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New York City was the national capital under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation_and_Perpetual_Union" title="Articles of Confederation and Perpetual Union">Articles of Confederation and Perpetual Union</a>, the first government. That organization was found to be insufficient, and prominent New Yorker <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a> advocated a new government that would include an executive, national courts, and the power to tax. Hamilton led the <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Convention_(1786)" title="Annapolis Convention (1786)">Annapolis Convention (1786)</a> that called for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Convention" title="Philadelphia Convention">Philadelphia Convention</a>, which drafted the United States Constitution, in which he also took part. The new government was to be a strong <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> national government to replace the relatively weaker <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a> of individual states. Following heated debate, which included the publication of the now quintessential constitutional interpretation—<i><a href="/wiki/The_Federalist_Papers" title="The Federalist Papers">The Federalist Papers</a></i>—as a series of installments in New York City newspapers, New York was the 11th state to ratify the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, on July 26, 1788.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> New York remained the national capital under the new constitution until 1790, and was the site of the inauguration of President George Washington, the drafting of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">United States Bill of Rights</a>, and the first session of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a>. Hamilton's revival of the heavily indebted United States economy after the war and the creation of a national bank significantly contributed to New York City becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_center" title="Financial center">financial center</a> of the new nation.</p>
<p>Both the Dutch and the British imported African slaves as laborers to the city and colony; New York had the second-highest population of slaves after Charleston, South Carolina. Slavery was extensive in New York City and some agricultural areas. The state passed a law for the gradual <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolition of slavery</a> soon after the Revolutionary War, but the last slave in New York was not freed until 1827.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="433" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg/220px-Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg/330px-Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lockport_bartlett_color_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lockport,_New_York" title="Lockport, New York">Lockport</a>, New York in 1839</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Transportation in western New York was by expensive wagons on muddy roads before canals opened up the rich farm lands to long-distance traffic. Governor <a href="/wiki/DeWitt_Clinton" title="DeWitt Clinton">DeWitt Clinton</a> promoted the Erie Canal that connected New York City to the Great Lakes, by the Hudson River, the new canal, and the rivers and lakes. Work commenced in 1817, and the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a> opened in 1825. <a href="/wiki/Packet_boat" title="Packet boat">Packet boats</a> pulled by horses on tow paths traveled slowly over the canal carrying passengers and freight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ErieCanal_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ErieCanal-57">[57]</a></sup> Farm products came in from the Midwest, and finished manufactured moved west. It was an engineering marvel which opened up vast areas of New York to commerce and settlement. It enabled Great Lakes port cities such as <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester</a> to grow and prosper. It also connected the burgeoning agricultural production of the Midwest and shipping on the Great Lakes, with the port of New York City. Improving transportation, it enabled additional population migration to territories west of New York. After 1850, railroads largely replaced the canal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>New York City was a major <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ocean port</a> and had extensive traffic importing cotton from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">South</a> and exporting manufacturing goods. Nearly half of the state's exports were related to cotton. Southern cotton factors, planters and bankers visited so often that they had favorite hotels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> At the same time, activism for <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">abolitionism</a> was strong upstate, where some communities provided stops on the <a href="/wiki/Underground_Railroad" title="Underground Railroad">Underground Railroad</a>. Upstate, and New York City, gave strong support for the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> In terms of finances, volunteer soldiers, and supplies. The state provided more than 370,000 soldiers to the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> armies. Over 53,000 New Yorkers died in service, roughly one of every seven who served. However, Irish draft riots in 1862 were a significant embarrassment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="930" data-file-width="1179" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg/220px-Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg/330px-Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg/440px-Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ellis_Island_in_1905.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a> in 1905</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:170px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:320px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv/320px--Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:320px;height:240px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="210.17663333333" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv.240p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="320" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="256848" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora&amp;quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file, 320 × 240 (663 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="320" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="662591" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv.160p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" data-height="160" data-bandwidth="129392" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;'><img alt="File:Ellis Island immigration footage.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv/170px--Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv.jpg" style="width:170px;height:128px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ellis_Island_immigration_footage.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Scenes at the Immigration Depot and a nearby dock on Ellis Island</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the early 19th century, New York City has been the largest <a href="/wiki/Port_of_entry" title="Port of entry">port of entry</a> for <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">legal immigration into the United States</a>. In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal government</a> did not assume direct jurisdiction for immigration until 1890. Prior to this time, the matter was delegated to the individual states, then via contract between the states and the federal government. Most immigrants to New York would disembark at the bustling docks along the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">East Rivers</a>, in the eventual <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>. On May 4, 1847 the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Legislature" title="New York State Legislature">New York State Legislature</a> created the Board of Commissioners of Immigration to regulate immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first permanent immigration depot in New York was established in 1855 at <a href="/wiki/Castle_Clinton" title="Castle Clinton">Castle Garden</a>, a converted <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> era fort located within what is now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_Park" title="Battery Park">Battery Park</a>, at the tip of Lower Manhattan. The first immigrants to arrive at the new depot were aboard three ships that had just been released from <a href="/wiki/Quarantine" title="Quarantine">quarantine</a>. Castle Garden served as New York's immigrant depot until it closed on April 18, 1890 when the federal government assumed control over immigration. During that period, more than 8 million immigrants passed through its doors (two out of every three U.S. immigrants).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the federal government assumed control, it established the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">Bureau of Immigration</a>, which chose the three-acre Ellis Island in <a href="/wiki/Upper_New_York_Bay" title="Upper New York Bay">Upper New York Harbor</a> for an entry depot. Already federally controlled, the island had served as an ammunition depot. It was chosen due its relative isolation with proximity to New York City and the rail lines of <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">Jersey City, New Jersey</a>, via a short ferry ride. While the island was being developed and expanded via <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>, the federal government operated a temporary depot at the Barge Office at the Battery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ellis Island opened on January 1, 1892, and operated as a central immigration center until the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1924" title="Immigration Act of 1924">National Origins Act</a> was passed in 1924, reducing immigration. After that date, the only immigrants to pass through were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Displaced_persons" title="Displaced persons">displaced persons</a> or war <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">refugees</a>. The island ceased all immigration processing on November 12, 1954 when the last person detained on the island, <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegian</a> seaman Arne Peterssen, was released. He had overstayed his shore leave and left on the 10:15 a.m. Manhattan-bound ferry to return to his ship.</p>
<p>More than 12 million immigrants passed through Ellis Island between 1892 and 1954. More than 100 million Americans across the United States can trace their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancestry" title="Ancestry">ancestry</a> to these immigrants.</p>
<p>Ellis Island was the subject of a contentious and long-running border and jurisdictional dispute between New York State and the State of New Jersey, as both claimed it. The issue was settled in 1998 by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a> which ruled that the original 3.3-acre (1.3 ha) island was New York State territory and that the balance of the 27.5 acres (11 ha) added after 1834 by landfill was in New Jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The island was added to the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> system in May 1965 by President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> and is still owned by the Federal government as part of the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty_National_Monument" title="Statue of Liberty National Monument">Statue of Liberty National Monument</a>. Ellis Island was opened to the public as a museum of immigration in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="September_11,_2001_attacks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="September_11.2C_2001_attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg"><img alt="Two talk gray, rectangular buildings spewing black smoke and flames, particularly from the left of the two." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="925" data-file-width="1063" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg/170px-UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg/255px-UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg/340px-UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UA_Flight_175_hits_WTC_south_tower_9-11_edit.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flight_175" title="Flight 175">Flight 175</a> hit the original <a href="/wiki/2_World_Trade_Center#Original_building_.281971.E2.80.932001.29" title="2 World Trade Center">South Tower</a> on September 11, 2001.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a></div>
<p>On September 11, 2001, two of four hijacked planes were flown into the Twin Towers of the original <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">World Trade Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, and the towers collapsed. <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a> also collapsed due to damage from fires. The other buildings of the World Trade Center complex were damaged beyond repair and demolished soon thereafter. The collapse of the Twin Towers caused extensive damage and resulted in the deaths of 2,753 victims, including 147 aboard the two planes. Since September 11, most of Lower Manhattan has been restored. In the years since, many rescue workers and residents of the area have developed several life-threatening illnesses, and some have died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>A memorial at the site, the <a href="/wiki/National_September_11_Memorial_%26_Museum" title="National September 11 Memorial &amp; Museum">National September 11 Memorial &amp; Museum</a>, was opened to the public on September 11, 2011. A permanent museum later opened at the site on March 21, 2014. Upon its completion in 2014, the new <a href="/wiki/One_World_Trade_Center" title="One World Trade Center">One World Trade Center</a> became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_New_York_City" title="List of tallest buildings in New York City">tallest skyscraper</a> in the Western Hemisphere, at 1,776 feet (541 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Other skyscrapers are under construction at the site.</p>
<h3><span id="Hurricane_Sandy,_2012"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Sandy.2C_2012">Hurricane Sandy, 2012</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Sandy_in_New_York" title="Effects of Hurricane Sandy in New York">Effects of Hurricane Sandy in New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG/220px-Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG/330px-Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG/440px-Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Sandy_Flooding_Avenue_C_2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flooding on <a href="/wiki/Avenue_C_(Manhattan)" title="Avenue C (Manhattan)">Avenue C</a> in Lower Manhattan caused by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On October 29 and 30, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> caused extensive destruction of the state's shorelines, ravaging portions of New York City and Long Island with record-high <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a>, with severe flooding and high winds causing <a href="/wiki/Power_outage" title="Power outage">power outages</a> for hundreds of thousands of New Yorkers, and leading to <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> shortages and disruption of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_transit" title="Mass transit">mass transit</a> systems. The storm and its profound effects have prompted the discussion of constructing <a href="/wiki/Seawall" title="Seawall">seawalls</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Coastal_management" title="Coastal management">coastal barriers</a> around the shorelines of New York City and Long Island to minimize the risk from another such future event. This is considered highly probable due to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and rise in sea levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LI_region_DEM-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="490" data-file-width="1023" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/LI_region_DEM-2.jpg/220px-LI_region_DEM-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/LI_region_DEM-2.jpg/330px-LI_region_DEM-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/LI_region_DEM-2.jpg/440px-LI_region_DEM-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LI_region_DEM-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Enveloped by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> alone are home to approximately 11 million residents conjointly.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1255" data-file-width="1643" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg/220px-Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg/330px-Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg/440px-Big_Slide_Mountain_from_Cascade.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_Mountains" title="Adirondack Mountains">Adirondack</a> <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_High_Peaks" title="Adirondack High Peaks">High Peaks</a> region.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_New_York" title="Geography of New York">Geography of New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="11195" data-file-width="14113" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg/180px-New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg/270px-New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg/360px-New_York_Relief_1-EDIT.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">New York <a href="/wiki/Terrain" title="Terrain">terrain</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hudsonmap.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="1005" data-file-width="1000" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hudsonmap.png/180px-Hudsonmap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hudsonmap.png/270px-Hudsonmap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hudsonmap.png/360px-Hudsonmap.png 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Map of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk</a> rivers.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles,_Onondaga_County,_New_York.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg/220px-Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg/330px-Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg/440px-Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles%2C_Onondaga_County%2C_New_York.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skaneateles_Lake_seen_from_the_village_of_Skaneateles,_Onondaga_County,_New_York.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Skaneateles_Lake" title="Skaneateles Lake">Skaneateles Lake</a>, one of the eleven <a href="/wiki/Finger_Lakes" title="Finger Lakes">Finger Lakes</a>, provides drinking water for the city of <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a> and nearby areas in <a href="/wiki/Central_New_York" title="Central New York">central New York</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New York covers 54,555 square miles (141,300 km<sup>2</sup>) and ranks as the 27th largest state by size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-area_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-area-3">[3]</a></sup> The highest elevation in New York is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Marcy" title="Mount Marcy">Mount Marcy</a> in the Adirondacks, at 5,344 feet (1,629 meters) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>; while the state's lowest point is at sea level, on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-usgs-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In contrast with New York City's urban landscape, the vast majority of the state's geographic area is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Meadow" title="Meadow">meadows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a>, rivers, farms, mountains, and lakes. Most of the southern part of the state rests on the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">Allegheny Plateau</a>, which extends from the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">southeastern United States</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Catskill_Mountains" title="Catskill Mountains">Catskill Mountains</a>; the section in New York State is known as the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Tier" title="Southern Tier">Southern Tier</a>. The rugged <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_Mountains" title="Adirondack Mountains">Adirondack Mountains</a>, with vast tracts of wilderness, lie west of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain_Valley" title="Lake Champlain Valley">Lake Champlain Valley</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Appalachian_Valley" title="Great Appalachian Valley">Great Appalachian Valley</a> dominates eastern New York and contains the Lake Champlain Valley as its northern half and the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a> as its southern half within the state. The <a href="/wiki/Tug_Hill" title="Tug Hill">Tug Hill</a> region arises as a <a href="/wiki/Cuesta" title="Cuesta">cuesta</a> east of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYS_THComm_Region_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYS_THComm_Region-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York"><i>Upstate</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Downstate_New_York" title="Downstate New York"><i>downstate</i></a> are often used informally to distinguish New York City or its greater metropolitan area from the rest of New York State. The placement of a boundary between the two is a matter of great contention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Unofficial and loosely defined regions of Upstate New York include the Southern Tier, which often includes the counties along the border with Pennsylvania,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Country_(New_York)" title="North Country (New York)">North Country</a>, which can mean anything from the strip along the Canada–US border to everything north of the Mohawk River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>New York contains a part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcellus_shale" title="Marcellus shale">Marcellus shale</a>, which extends into Ohio and Pennsylvania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frack_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-frack-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Borders">Borders</span></h4>
<p>Of New York State's total area, 13.6% consists of water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Much of New York's boundaries are in water, as is true for New York City: four of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" title="Borough (New York City)">five boroughs</a> are situated on three islands at the mouth of the Hudson River: <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan Island</a>; <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, which contains <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> at its western end. The state's borders include a water boundary in (clockwise from the west) two <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a> and Lake Ontario, which are connected by the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">Niagara River</a>); the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, with New York and Ontario sharing the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Islands" title="Thousand Islands">Thousand Islands</a> <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> within the Saint Lawrence River, while most of its border with Quebec is on land; it shares <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Lake Champlain</a> with the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> state of Vermont; the New England state of Massachusetts has mostly a land border, while Connecticut has land and sea borders; New York extends into <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Sound" title="Long Island Sound">Long Island Sound</a> and the Atlantic Ocean, sharing a water border with <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>. Except for areas near the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a>, New York has a mostly land boarder with two <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic</a> states, New Jersey and Pennsylvania. New York is the only state that includes within its borders parts of the Great Lakes and the Atlantic Ocean.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drainage">Drainage</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> begins near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tear_of_the_Clouds" title="Lake Tear of the Clouds">Lake Tear of the Clouds</a> and flows south through the eastern part of the state, without draining Lakes <a href="/wiki/Lake_George_(New_York)" title="Lake George (New York)">George</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Champlain</a>. Lake George empties at its north end into Lake Champlain, whose northern end extends into Canada, where it drains into the <a href="/wiki/Richelieu_River" title="Richelieu River">Richelieu River</a> and then ultimately the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence River</a>. The western section of the state is drained by the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> and rivers of the <a href="/wiki/Susquehanna_River" title="Susquehanna River">Susquehanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a> systems. <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">Niagara Falls</a> is shared between New York and Ontario as it flows on the Niagara River from Lake Erie to Lake Ontario. The Delaware River Basin Compact, signed in 1961 by New York, New Jersey, Pennsylvania, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, and the federal government, regulates the utilization of water of the Delaware system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_New_York" title="Climate of New York">Climate of New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="773" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif/220px-LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif/330px-LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif/440px-LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LakeEffectSnowBuffalo101206.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">Lake-effect snow</a> is a major contributor to heavy snowfall totals in <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">western New York</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Tug_Hill" title="Tug Hill">Tug Hill</a> region.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In general, New York has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>, though under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, New York City has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYClimate_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYClimate-79">[79]</a></sup> Weather in New York is heavily influenced by two continental air masses: a warm, humid one from the southwest and a cold, dry one from the northwest.</p>
<p>Downstate New York, comprising New York City, Long Island, and lower portions of the Hudson Valley, has rather warm summers, with some periods of high humidity, and cold, damp winters which, however, are relatively mild compared to temperatures in Upstate New York, secondary to the former region's lower elevation, proximity to the Atlantic Ocean, and relatively lower <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> compared to the latter. Upstate New York experiences warm summers, marred by only occasional, brief intervals of sultry conditions, with long and cold winters. Western New York, particularly the Tug Hill region, receives heavy <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">lake-effect snows</a>, especially during the earlier portions of winter, before the surface of Lake Ontario itself is covered by ice. The summer climate is cool in the Adirondacks, Catskills, and at higher elevations of the Southern Tier.</p>
<p>Summer daytime temperatures usually range from the upper 70s to mid-80s °F (25 to 30 °C), over much of the state. In the majority of winter seasons, a temperature of −13 °F (−25 °C) or lower can be expected in the northern highlands (Northern Plateau) and 5 °F (−15 °C) or colder in the southwestern and east-central highlands of the Southern Tier.</p>
<p>New York ranks 46th among the 50 states in the amount of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> generated per person. This relative <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">efficient energy usage</a> is primarily due to the dense, compact settlement in the New York City metropolitan area, and the state population's high rate of <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">mass transit</a> use in this area and between major cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States#New_York" title="List of regions of the United States">List of regions of the United States § New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="476" data-file-width="633" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg/220px-Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg/330px-Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg/440px-Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_New_York_Economic_Regions.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Economic regions of New York</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due to its long history, New York has several overlapping and often conflicting definitions of regions within the state. The regions are also not fully definable due to colloquial use of regional labels. The New York State Department of Economic Development provides two distinct definitions of these regions; it divides the state into ten economic regions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> which approximately correspond to terminology used by residents:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-4" style="-moz-column-count: 4; -webkit-column-count: 4; column-count: 4;">
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">Western New York</a></li>
