<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_parks">State parks</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_state_parks" title="List of New York state parks">List of New York state parks</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Office_of_Parks,_Recreation_and_Historic_Preservation" title="New York State Office of Parks, Recreation and Historic Preservation">New York State Office of Parks, Recreation and Historic Preservation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="936" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg/170px-Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg/255px-Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg/340px-Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adirondack_and_Catskill_Parks_Locator.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two major state parks (in green) are the <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_Park" title="Adirondack Park">Adirondack Park</a> (north) and the <a href="/wiki/Catskill_Park" title="Catskill Park">Catskill Park</a> (south).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New York has many state parks and two major forest preserves. <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls_State_Park" title="Niagara Falls State Park">Niagara Falls State Park</a>, established in 1885, is the oldest state park in the United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSA_EnvHist_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSA_EnvHist-83">[83]</a></sup> and the first to be created via <a href="/wiki/Eminent_domain" title="Eminent domain">eminent domain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NFSP_NPS_study_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-NFSP_NPS_study-84">[84]</a></sup> In 1892, <a href="/wiki/Adirondack_Park" title="Adirondack Park">Adirondack Park</a>, roughly the size of the state of <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> and the largest state park in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lakeplacid.com_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-lakeplacid.com-85">[85]</a></sup> was established and given state constitutional protection to remain "forever wild" in 1894. The park is larger than <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Everglades_National_Park" title="Everglades National Park">Everglades</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glacier_National_Park_(U.S.)" title="Glacier National Park (U.S.)">Glacier</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon_National_Park" title="Grand Canyon National Park">Grand Canyon</a> national parks combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lakeplacid.com_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-lakeplacid.com-85">[85]</a></sup> It is larger than the <a href="/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park" title="Yellowstone National Park">Yellowstone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yosemite_National_Park" title="Yosemite National Park">Yosemite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glacier_National_Park_(U.S.)" title="Glacier National Park (U.S.)">Glacier</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Olympic_National_Park" title="Olympic National Park">Olympic National Parks</a> combined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Catskill_Park" title="Catskill Park">Catskill Park</a> was protected in legislation passed in 1885,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatskillPark1_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-CatskillPark1-87">[87]</a></sup> which declared that its land was to be conserved and never put up for sale or lease. Consisting of 700,000 acres (2,800 km<sup>2</sup>) of land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatskillPark1_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-CatskillPark1-87">[87]</a></sup> the park is a habitat for deer, <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">minks</a>, and fishers. There are some 400 <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">black bears</a> living in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The state operates numerous campgrounds, and there are over 300 miles (480 km) of multi-use trails in the Park.</p>
<p>The 1797 <a href="/wiki/Montauk_Point_Light" title="Montauk Point Light">Montauk Lighthouse</a>, commissioned under <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>, is a major tourist attraction in <a href="/wiki/Montauk_State_Park" title="Montauk State Park">Montauk State Park</a> at the easternmost tip of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hither_Hills_State_Park" title="Hither Hills State Park">Hither Hills State Park</a>, also on the <a href="/wiki/South_Fork_(Long_Island)" title="South Fork (Long Island)">South Fork</a> of Long Island, offers camping and is a popular destination with surfcasting sport fishermen.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="National_parks,_monuments,_and_historic_landmarks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="National_parks.2C_monuments.2C_and_historic_landmarks">National parks, monuments, and historic landmarks</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Liberty,_NY.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2668" data-file-width="3558" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg/200px-Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg/300px-Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg/400px-Statue_of_Liberty%2C_NY.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a> is a symbol of the United States and its ideals of freedom, <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, and opportunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="309" data-file-width="432" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg/200px-African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg/300px-African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg/400px-African_Burial_Ground-aerial_view-NYC.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/African_Burial_Ground_National_Monument" title="African Burial Ground National Monument">African Burial Ground National Monument</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG/200px-GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG/300px-GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG/400px-GeneralSchylerHouse.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Philip_Schuyler" title="Philip Schuyler">General Shuyler's</a> house at <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_National_Historical_Park" title="Saratoga National Historical Park">Saratoga National Historical Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The State of New York is well represented in the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park System</a> with 22 <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a>, which received 16,349,381 visitors in 2011. In addition, there are 4 <a href="/wiki/National_Heritage_Area" title="National Heritage Area">National Heritage Areas</a>, 27 <a href="/wiki/National_Natural_Landmark" title="National Natural Landmark">National Natural Landmarks</a>, 262 <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmarks</a>, and 5,379 listings on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Burial_Ground_National_Monument" title="African Burial Ground National Monument">African Burial Ground National Monument</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a> is the only National Monument dedicated to Americans of African ancestry. It preserves a site containing the remains of more than 400 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">Africans</a> buried during the late 17th and 18th centuries in a portion of what was the largest colonial-era cemetery for people of African descent, both free and enslaved, with an estimated tens of thousands of remains interred. The site's excavation and study were called "the most important historic urban archeological project in the United States."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABG_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABG-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fire_Island_National_Seashore" title="Fire Island National Seashore">Fire Island National Seashore</a> is a <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_national_lakeshores_and_seashores" title="List of United States national lakeshores and seashores">National Seashore</a> that protects a 26-mile (42 km) section of <a href="/wiki/Fire_Island" title="Fire Island">Fire Island</a>, an approximately 30-mile (48 km) long <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">barrier island</a> separated from the mainland of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Great_South_Bay" title="Great South Bay">Great South Bay</a>. The island is part of <a href="/wiki/Suffolk_County,_New_York" title="Suffolk County, New York">Suffolk County</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gateway_National_Recreation_Area" title="Gateway National Recreation Area">Gateway National Recreation Area</a> is more than 26,000 acres (10,522 ha) of water, <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh" title="Salt marsh">salt marsh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wetlands" title="Wetlands">wetlands</a>, islands, and shoreline at the entrance to New York Harbor, the majority of which lies within New York. Including areas on Long Island and in New Jersey, it covers more area than that of two Manhattan Islands.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Grant_National_Memorial" title="General Grant National Memorial">General Grant National Memorial</a> is the final resting place of President <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> and is the largest <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum" title="Mausoleum">mausoleum</a> in North America.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Grange_National_Memorial" title="Hamilton Grange National Memorial">Hamilton Grange National Memorial</a> preserves the home of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>, Caribbean immigrant and <a href="/wiki/Orphan" title="Orphan">orphan</a> who rose to be a United States founding father and associate of George Washington.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Home_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site" title="Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site">Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site</a>, established in 1945, preserves the Springwood estate in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_New_York" title="Hyde Park, New York">Hyde Park, New York</a>. Springwood was the birthplace, lifelong home, and burial place of the 32nd <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls_National_Heritage_Area" title="Niagara Falls National Heritage Area">Niagara Falls National Heritage Area</a> was designated by Congress in 2008; it stretches from the western boundary of <a href="/wiki/Wheatfield,_New_York" title="Wheatfield, New York">Wheatfield, New York</a> to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_River" title="Niagara River">Niagara River</a> on Lake <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, including the communities of Niagara Falls, Youngstown, and Lewiston. It includes <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls_State_Park" title="Niagara Falls State Park">Niagara Falls State Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Niagara" title="Fort Niagara">Colonial Niagara Historic District</a>. It is managed in collaboration with the state.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saratoga_National_Historical_Park" title="Saratoga National Historical Park">Saratoga National Historical Park</a> preserves the site of the <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Saratoga" title="Battles of Saratoga">Battles of Saratoga</a>, the first significant American military victory of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. In 1777, American forces defeated a major <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, which led <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to recognize the independence of the United States, and enter the war as a decisive military ally of the struggling Americans.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty_National_Monument" title="Statue of Liberty National Monument">Statue of Liberty National Monument</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">Statue of Liberty</a>. The statue, designed by <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Auguste_Bartholdi" title="Frédéric Auguste Bartholdi">Frédéric Bartholdi</a>, was a gift from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to the United States to mark the Centennial of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_the_United_States" title="Declaration of Independence of the United States">American Declaration of Independence</a>; it was dedicated in New York Harbor on October 28, 1886. It has since become an icon of the United States and the concepts of democracy and freedom.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stonewall_National_Monument" title="Stonewall National Monument">Stonewall National Monument</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a> neighborhood of Lower Manhattan, is the first U.S. National Monument dedicated to <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States" title="LGBT rights in the United States">LGBTQ rights</a>, designated on June 24, 2016. The monument comprises the <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_Inn" title="Stonewall Inn">Stonewall Inn</a>, commonly recognized to be the cradle of the <a href="/wiki/Gay_liberation" title="Gay liberation">gay liberation</a> movement as the site of the 1969 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stonewall_Riots" title="Stonewall Riots">Stonewall Riots</a>; the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Street" title="Christopher Street">Christopher Park</a>; and surrounding streets and sidewalks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GayGreenwichVillage1_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-GayGreenwichVillage1-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GayGreenwichVillage2_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-GayGreenwichVillage2-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GayGreenwichVillage3_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-GayGreenwichVillage3-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt_Birthplace_National_Historic_Site" title="Theodore Roosevelt Birthplace National Historic Site">Theodore Roosevelt Birthplace National Historic Site</a> is the birthplace and childhood home of President Theodore Roosevelt, the only US President born in New York City before <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Counties.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="763" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_York_Counties.svg/170px-New_York_Counties.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_York_Counties.svg/255px-New_York_Counties.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_York_Counties.svg/340px-New_York_Counties.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Counties.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the counties in New York</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_New_York" title="Administrative divisions of New York">Administrative divisions of New York</a></div>
<p>New York is divided into 62 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Aside from the five counties of New York City, each of these counties is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Town#New_York" title="Town">towns</a> and <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a>, incorporated under state law. Towns can contain incorporated <a href="/wiki/Village" title="Village">villages</a> or unincorporated <a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(place)#New_York" title="Hamlet (place)">hamlets</a>. New York City is divided into five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" title="Borough (New York City)">boroughs</a>, each coterminous with a county.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Downstate_New_York" title="Downstate New York">Downstate New York</a> (<a href="/wiki/Geography_of_New_York_City" title="Geography of New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, and the southern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a>) can be considered to form the central core of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">Northeast megalopolis</a>, an urbanized region stretching from <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> to <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.</p>
<p>The major cities of the state developed along the key transportation and <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> of the early 19th century, including the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a> and railroads paralleling it. Today, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Thruway" title="New York Thruway">New York Thruway</a> acts as a modern counterpart to commercial water routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics_of_New_York" title="Demographics of New York">Demographics of New York</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Population_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/New_York_Population_Map.png/170px-New_York_Population_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/New_York_Population_Map.png/255px-New_York_Population_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/New_York_Population_Map.png/340px-New_York_Population_Map.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Population_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New York population distribution map</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The distribution of change in population growth is uneven in New York State; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_metropolitan_area" title="New York City metropolitan area">New York City metropolitan area</a> is growing considerably, along with <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_County,_New_York" title="Saratoga County, New York">Saratoga County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016NYCountyGrowthCensus_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-2016NYCountyGrowthCensus-97">[97]</a></sup> New York City gained more residents between April 2010 and July 2014 (316,000) than any other U.S. city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014NYCest_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014NYCest-98">[98]</a></sup> Conversely, outside of the <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca</a> area, population growth in much of <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">Western New York</a> is nearly stagnant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016NYCountyGrowthCensus_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016NYCountyGrowthCensus-97">[97]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> statistics, the state is a leading recipient of migrants from around the globe. Between 2000 and 2005, immigration failed to surpass emigration, a trend that has been reversing since 2006. New York State lost two House seats in the 2011 congressional reapportionment, secondary to relatively slow growth when compared to the rest of the United States. In 2000 and 2005, more people moved from New York to <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> than from any one state to another, contributing to New York becoming the U.S.'s fourth most populous state in 2015, behind Florida, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> However, New York State has the second-largest international immigrant population in the country among the American states, at 4.2 million as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>; most reside in and around New York City, due to its size, high profile, vibrant economy, and <a href="/wiki/Cosmopolitanism" title="Cosmopolitanism">cosmopolitan</a> culture.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of New York was 19,795,791 on July 1, 2015, a 2.16% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-9">[9]</a></sup> Despite the open land in the state, New York's population is very urban, with 92% of residents living in an urban area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> predominantly in the New York City metropolitan area.</p>
<p>Two-thirds of New York State's population resides in New York City Metropolitan Area. New York City is the most populous city in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> with an estimated record high population of 8,550,405 in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCest2_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYCest2-10">[10]</a></sup> incorporating more immigration into the city than emigration since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inmigration_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-inmigration-102">[102]</a></sup> More than twice as many people live in New York City as in the second-most populous U.S. city (<a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> and within a smaller area. <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> alone accounted for a Census-estimated 7,838,722 residents in 2015, representing 39.6% of New York State's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCest2_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYCest2-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kings_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kings_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queens_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queens_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nassau_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nassau_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suffolk_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Suffolk_County.2C_New_York_QuickFacts-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>6.5% of New York's population were under five years of age, 24.7% under 18, and 12.9% were 65 or older. Females made up 51.8% of the state's population.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_populous_counties">Most populous counties</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_New_York" title="List of counties in New York">List of counties in New York</a></div>
<p>These are the ten counties with the largest populations as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCounties_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCounties-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCensusfacts_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCensusfacts-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Kings County</a> (Brooklyn): 2,504,700</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens County</a> (Queens): 2,230,722</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">New York County</a> (Manhattan): 1,585,873</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suffolk_County,_New_York" title="Suffolk County, New York">Suffolk County</a>: 1,493,350</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">Bronx County</a> (the Bronx): 1,385,108</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_New_York" title="Nassau County, New York">Nassau County</a>: 1,339,532</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">Westchester County</a>: 949,113</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erie_County,_New_York" title="Erie County, New York">Erie County</a>: 919,040</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_New_York" title="Monroe County, New York">Monroe County</a>: 744,344</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Richmond County</a> (Staten Island): 468,730</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities">Major cities</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_New_York" title="List of cities in New York">List of cities in New York</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_in_New_York" title="List of towns in New York">List of towns in New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_villages_in_New_York" title="List of villages in New York">List of villages in New York</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_census-designated_places_in_New_York" title="List of census-designated places in New York">List of census-designated places in New York</a></div>
<p>There are 62 cities in New York. The largest city in the state and the most populous city in the United States is New York City, which comprises five counties (each coextensive with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" title="Borough (New York City)">borough</a>): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronx" title="Bronx">Bronx</a>, New York County (<a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, Kings County (<a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>), and Richmond County (<a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a>). New York City is home to more than two-fifths of the state's population. <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>, the state capital, is the sixth-largest city in New York State. The smallest city is <a href="/wiki/Sherrill,_New_York" title="Sherrill, New York">Sherrill, New York</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Oneida_County,_New_York" title="Oneida County, New York">Oneida County</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hempstead,_New_York" title="Hempstead, New York">Hempstead</a> is the most populous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_(New_York)" title="Town (New York)">town</a> in the state; if it were a city, it would be the second largest in New York State, with over 700,000 residents.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_areas">Metropolitan areas</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_York_statistical_areas" title="New York statistical areas">New York statistical areas</a></div>
<p>The following are the top ten <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan areas</a> in the state as of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York City, Long Island, and the Hudson Valley</a> (19,567,410 in NY/<a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">NJ</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">PA</a>, 13,038,826 in NY)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buffalo%E2%80%93Niagara_Falls_metropolitan_area" title="Buffalo–Niagara Falls metropolitan area">Buffalo-Niagara Falls</a> (1,135,509)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York_metropolitan_area" title="Rochester, New York metropolitan area">Rochester</a> (1,079,671)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Capital_District,_New_York" title="Capital District, New York">Albany and the Capital District</a> (870,716)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Syracuse_metropolitan_area" title="Syracuse metropolitan area">Syracuse</a> (662,577)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utica-Rome_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Utica-Rome Metropolitan Statistical Area">Utica-Rome</a> (299,397)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Binghamton_metropolitan_area" title="Binghamton metropolitan area">Binghamton</a> (251,725)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingston,_New_York_metropolitan_area" title="Kingston, New York metropolitan area">Kingston</a> (182,493)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glens_Falls_metropolitan_area" title="Glens Falls metropolitan area">Glens Falls</a> (128,923)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watertown,_New_York_metropolitan_area" title="Watertown, New York metropolitan area">Watertown-Fort Drum</a> (116,229)</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_and_ethnicity">Race and ethnicity</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;max-width:229px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG/225px-Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG/338px-Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG/450px-Chinatown_manhattan_2009.JPG 2x" width="225"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Chinatown.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1024" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brooklyn_Chinatown.png/225px-Brooklyn_Chinatown.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brooklyn_Chinatown.png/338px-Brooklyn_Chinatown.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brooklyn_Chinatown.png/450px-Brooklyn_Chinatown.png 2x" width="225"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Manhattan Chinatown (紐約華埠)</a>, home to the highest concentration of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese people</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> at top, and one of several <a href="/wiki/Chinatowns_in_Brooklyn" title="Chinatowns in Brooklyn">Chinatowns in Brooklyn (布魯克林華埠)</a> below. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Americans_in_New_York_City" title="Chinese Americans in New York City">Chinese in New York</a> constitute the fastest-growing nationality in New York State and on Long Island,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigrants2013est_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Immigrants2013est-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Immigrants2012est_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Immigrants2012est-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2013est_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2013est-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2012est_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2012est-115">[115]</a></sup> with large-scale <a href="/wiki/Chinese_emigration" title="Chinese emigration">Chinese immigration</a> continuing into New York.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The racial makeup of New York State as of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a> was:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census2010_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Census2010-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a>: 65.7% (58.3% <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">non-Hispanic</a>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_American" title="Black American">Black or African American</a>: 15.9%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian and Alaska Native</a>: 0.6%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">Asian</a>: 7.3%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">Native Hawaiian and other Pacific Islander</a>: approx. 0.0%</li>
<li>Other race: 7.4%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 3.0%</li>
</ul>

<p><a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> of any race were 17.6% of the population in 2010: 2.4% were of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexican</a>, 5.5% <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Rican</a>, 0.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">Cuban</a>, and 9.4% other Hispanic or Latino origin. According to the 2010–2015 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>, the largest ancestry groups were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian</a> (13.0%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> (12.1%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> (10.3%), <a href="/wiki/American_ancestry" title="American ancestry">American</a> (5.4%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> (5.2%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="470" data-file-width="609" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG/220px-Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG/330px-Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG/440px-Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ancestry-new-york-by_county-2000.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New York population ethnicity map</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state's most populous racial group, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">non-Hispanic white</a>, has declined as a proportion of the state population from 94.6% in 1940 to 58.3% in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopUS_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopUS-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-census1-117">[117]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 55.6% of New York's population younger than age 1 were minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> New York's robustly increasing <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> population, the largest outside of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> was the highest among states both by percentage and absolute number in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> It is driven by the high reproductive rate of <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox Jewish</a> families,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> particularly in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> and communities of the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a>.</p>
<p>New York is home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_African-American_population" title="List of U.S. states by African-American population">second-largest African American</a> population (after <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Asian_Americans" title="Demographics of Asian Americans">second largest Asian-American</a> population (after <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>) in the United States. New York's uniracial Black population increased by 2.0% between 2000 and 2010, to 3,073,800.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYQuickLinks_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYQuickLinks-125">[125]</a></sup> The Black population is in a state of flux, as New York is the largest recipient of immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2013est_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2013est-114">[114]</a></sup> while established African Americans are migrating out of New York to the <a href="/wiki/New_Great_Migration" title="New Great Migration">southern United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The New York City neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a> has historically been a major cultural capital for African-Americans of sub-Saharan descent, and <a href="/wiki/Bedford%E2%80%93Stuyvesant,_Brooklyn" title="Bedford–Stuyvesant, Brooklyn">Bedford-Stuyvesant</a> in Brooklyn has the largest such population in the United States. Meanwhile, New York's uniracial Asian population increased by a notable 36% from 2000 to 2010, to 1,420,244.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYQuickLinks_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYQuickLinks-125">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, in New York City, is home to the state's largest Asian-American population and is the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_diversity" title="Ethnic diversity">ethnically diverse</a> county in the United States; it is the most ethnically diverse urban area in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>New York's growing uniracial Hispanic-or-Latino population numbered 3,416,922 in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> a 19% increase from the 2,867,583 enumerated in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Queens is home to the largest <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_American" title="Colombian American">Colombian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_American" title="Ecuadorian American">Ecuadorian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peruvian_American" title="Peruvian American">Peruvian</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_American" title="Bolivian American">Bolivian</a>) populations in the United States. In addition, New York has the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_people" title="Puerto Rican people">Puerto Rican</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_American" title="Dominican American">Dominican</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_American" title="Jamaican American">Jamaican American</a> populations in the continental United States.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> population constitutes the fastest-growing nationality in New York State; multiple <a href="/wiki/Natural_satellite" title="Natural satellite">satellites</a> of the original <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Manhattan Chinatown (曼哈頓華埠)</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Brooklyn" title="Chinatown, Brooklyn">Brooklyn (布鲁克林華埠)</a>, and around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Flushing" title="Chinatown, Flushing">Flushing, Queens (法拉盛華埠)</a>, are thriving as traditionally urban enclaves, while also expanding rapidly eastward into suburban <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_New_York" title="Nassau County, New York">Nassau County (拿騷縣)</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island (長島)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> New York State has become the top destination for new Chinese immigrants, and large-scale <a href="/wiki/Chinese_emigration" title="Chinese emigration">Chinese immigration</a> continues into the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2013est_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2013est-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2012est_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2012est-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2011est_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2011est-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chinese2010est_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chinese2010est-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> A new <a href="/wiki/China_City_of_America" title="China City of America">China City of America</a> is also planned in <a href="/wiki/Sullivan_County,_New_York" title="Sullivan County, New York">Sullivan County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Long Island, including Queens and Nassau County, is also home to several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curry_Hill" title="Curry Hill">Little Indias (लघु भारत)</a> and a large <a href="/wiki/Koreatown,_Long_Island" title="Koreatown, Long Island">Koreatown (롱 아일랜드 코리아타운)</a>, with large and growing attendant populations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_American" title="Indian American">Indian Americans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">Korean Americans</a>, respectively. Brooklyn has been a destination for <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> immigrants of African descent, as well as Asian Indian immigrants.</p>
<p>In the 2000 Census, New York had the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian American</a> population, composing the largest self-identified ancestral group in <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">Staten Island</a> and Long Island, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish Americans</a>. Albany and the <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_Valley" title="Mohawk Valley">Mohawk Valley</a> also have large communities of ethnic Italians and Irish Americans, reflecting 19th and early 20th-century immigration. In <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo</a> and western New York, <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German Americans</a> comprise the largest ancestry. In the <a href="/wiki/North_Country_(New_York)" title="North Country (New York)">North Country</a> of New York, <a href="/wiki/French_Canadians" title="French Canadians">French Canadians</a> represent the leading ethnicity, given the area's proximity to <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>. Americans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> ancestry are present throughout all of upstate New York, reflecting early colonial and later immigrants.</p>

<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a></td>
<td>0.53%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a></td>
<td>0.43%</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 2010, the most common <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> spoken in New York, besides <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_American_English" title="General American English">General American English</a>, were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_dialect" title="New York dialect">New York City area dialect</a> (including <a href="/wiki/New_York_Latino_English" title="New York Latino English">New York Latino English</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_English_dialects#North_Jersey_English" title="New Jersey English dialects">North Jersey English</a>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_New_England_dialect" title="Western New England dialect">Western New England accent</a> around <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inland_Northern_American_English" title="Inland Northern American English">Inland Northern American English</a> in Buffalo and western New York State. As many as 800 languages are spoken in New York City,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-800source2_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-800source2-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-800source3_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-800source3-140">[140]</a></sup> making it the most linguistically diverse city in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 70.72% (12,788,233) of New York residents aged five and older reported speaking only <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home, while 14.44% (2,611,903) spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 2.61% (472,955) <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> (which includes <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">Mandarin</a>), 1.20% (216,468) <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, 1.18% (213,785) <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, 0.79% (142,169) <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French Creole</a>, 0.75% (135,789) <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, 0.67% (121,917) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a>, 0.63% (114,574) <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> was spoken by 0.53% (95,413) of the population over the age of five. In total, 29.28% (5,295,016) of New York's population aged five and older reported speaking a language other than English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(November 2016)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (ARDA) reported that the largest denominations were the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> with 6,286,916; <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox Judaism</a> with 588,500; <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> with 392,953; and the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> with 328,315 adherents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-142">[142]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation_and_gender_identity">Sexual orientation and gender identity</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_York" title="Same-sex marriage in New York">Same-sex marriage in New York</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LGBTQ_culture_in_New_York_City" title="LGBTQ culture in New York City">LGBTQ culture in New York City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg/200px-Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg/300px-Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg/400px-Capital_Gay_Pride_parade_in_Albany_New_York_2009.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_(13563189244).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2805" data-file-width="3143" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg/200px-Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg/300px-Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg/400px-Model_Geena_Rocero_Coming_out_Transgender_%2813563189244%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">Gay pride</a> parade, <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany</a> at top, and <a href="/wiki/International_Transgender_Day_of_Visibility" title="International Transgender Day of Visibility">International Transgender Day of Visibility</a> introduced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_the_New_York_City_metropolitan_region" title="Filipinos in the New York City metropolitan region">Manila</a>-born <a href="/wiki/Geena_Rocero" title="Geena Rocero">Geena Rocero</a> in New York City below.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Roughly 3.8 percent of the state's adult population self-identifies as <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">gay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a>. This constitutes a total LGBT adult population of 570,388 individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> In 2010, the number of same-sex couple households stood at roughly 48,932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> New York was the fifth state to license <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_York" title="Same-sex marriage in New York">same-sex marriages</a>, after New Hampshire. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bloomberg" title="Michael Bloomberg">Michael Bloomberg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_New_York_City" title="Mayor of New York City">Mayor of New York City</a>, stated that "same-sex marriages in New York City have generated an estimated $259 million in economic impact and $16 million in City revenues" in the first year after the enactment of the Marriage Equality Act".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_New_York" title="Same-sex marriage in New York">Same-sex marriages in New York</a> were legalized on June 24, 2011 and were authorized to take place beginning 30 days thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> New York City is also home to the largest <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> population in the United States, estimated at 25,000 in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_Pride_March" title="New York City Pride March">New York City Pride March</a> (or <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_LGBT_Pride_March" title="New York City LGBT Pride March">gay</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pride_march" title="Pride march">pride parade</a>) traverses southward down <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Avenue" title="Fifth Avenue">Fifth Avenue</a> in Manhattan, ending at <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a>, and rivals the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo_Gay_Pride_Parade" title="Sao Paulo Gay Pride Parade">Sao Paulo Gay Pride Parade</a> as the largest pride parade in the world, attracting tens of thousands of participants and millions of sidewalk spectators each June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCWorld.27sLargestPrideParade_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCWorld.27sLargestPrideParade-151">[151]</a></sup> In June 2017, plans were announced for the first official monument to LGBT individuals commissioned by the State of New York, in contrast to the <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_National_Monument" title="Stonewall National Monument">Stonewall National Monument</a>, which was commissioned by the U.S. federal government. The State monument is planned to be built in <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River_Park" title="Hudson River Park">Hudson River Park</a> in Manhattan, near the waterfront Hudson River <a href="/wiki/Pier" title="Pier">piers</a> which have served as historically significant symbols of New York's role as a meeting place and a safe haven for LGBT communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSOfficialLGBTMonument_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSOfficialLGBTMonument-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_York_(state)" title="Economy of New York (state)">Economy of New York (state)</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="New York locations by per capita income">New York locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYC_NYSE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2958" data-file-width="2524" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NYC_NYSE.jpg/170px-NYC_NYSE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NYC_NYSE.jpg/255px-NYC_NYSE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/NYC_NYSE.jpg/340px-NYC_NYSE.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">

<a href="/wiki/Silicon_Alley" title="Silicon Alley">Silicon Alley</a> has expanded well beyond its cradle in the <a href="/wiki/Flatiron_District" title="Flatiron District">Flatiron District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="1000" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg/220px-ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg/330px-ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg/440px-ChryslerBuildingMidtownManhattanNewYorkCity.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a> in New York City, the largest <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> in the world.</div>

</div>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="400" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg/220px-Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg/330px-Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Cold_Spring_Harbor_Laboratory.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
