</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/220px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/330px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/440px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a> in Midtown Manhattan, hub of the <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theater_District_(Manhattan)" title="Theater District (Manhattan)">theater district</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Media_(communication)" title="Media (communication)">media</a> center, and one of the world's busiest <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian" title="Pedestrian">pedestrian</a> intersections.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New York's <a href="/wiki/Comparison_between_U.S._states_and_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="Comparison between U.S. states and countries by GDP (nominal)">gross state product</a> in 2015 was $1.44 trillion. If New York State were an independent nation, it would rank as the 12th or 13th largest economy in the world, depending upon international <a href="/wiki/Currency_money" title="Currency money">currency</a> fluctuations. However, in 2013, the multi-state, New York City-centered <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> produced a <a href="/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product" title="Gross metropolitan product">gross metropolitan product</a> (GMP) of nearly US$1.4 trillion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> while in 2012, the corresponding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Combined Statistical Areas">Combined Statistical Area</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> generated a GMP of over US$1.55 trillion, both ranking first nationally by a wide margin and behind the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> of only twelve nations and eleven nations, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wall_Street">Wall Street</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a></div>
<p>Anchored by Wall Street in the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">Financial District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, New York City has been called both the most economically powerful city and the leading financial center of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomicallyPowerful2015_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-EconomicallyPowerful2015-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Lower Manhattan is the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> in the United States and is home to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a>, on Wall Street, and the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a>, at <a href="/wiki/One_Liberty_Plaza" title="One Liberty Plaza">165 Broadway</a>, representing the world's largest and second largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchanges</a>, respectively, as measured both by overall average daily trading volume and by total <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> of their listed companies in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSEhighestcap_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYSEhighestcap-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSElargest_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSElargest-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">Investment banking</a> fees on Wall Street totaled approximately $40 billion in 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> while in 2013, senior New York City bank officers who manage <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk and compliance</a> functions earned as much as $324,000 annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> In fiscal year 2013–14, Wall Street's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Securities_industry" title="Securities industry">securities industry</a> generated 19% of New York State's tax revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> New York City remains the largest global center for trading in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_equity" title="Public equity">public equity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">debt</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_markets" title="Capital markets">capital markets</a>, driven in part by the size and <a href="/wiki/Financial_Development_Index" title="Financial Development Index">financial development</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._economy" title="U.S. economy">U.S. economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNY2007_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNY2007-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:31–32</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> New York also leads in <a href="/wiki/Hedge_fund" title="Hedge fund">hedge fund</a> management; <a href="/wiki/List_of_private_equity_firms" title="List of private equity firms">private equity</a>; and the monetary volume of <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">mergers and acquisitions</a>. Several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Investment_Banking" title="Investment Banking">investment banks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Investment_management" title="Investment management">investment managers</a> headquartered in Manhattan are important participants in other global financial centers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNY2007_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNY2007-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:34–35</sup> New York is also the principal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_banking" title="Commercial banking">commercial banking</a> center of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Media_conglomerate" title="Media conglomerate">media conglomerates</a> are also based in the city. <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> contained approximately 520 million square feet (48.1 million m<sup>2</sup>) of office space in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> making it the largest office market in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a> is the largest central business district in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Silicon_Alley">Silicon Alley</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Alley" title="Silicon Alley">Silicon Alley</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tech_companies_in_New_York" title="Tech companies in New York">Tech companies in New York</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biotech_and_pharmaceutical_companies_in_New_York" title="Biotech and pharmaceutical companies in New York">Biotech and pharmaceutical companies in New York</a></div>
<p>Silicon Alley, centered in New York City, has evolved into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metonym" title="Metonym">metonym</a> for the sphere encompassing the New York City metropolitan region's <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship_ecosystem" title="Entrepreneurship ecosystem">high technology and entrepreneurship ecosystem</a>; in 2015, Silicon Alley generated over US$7.3 billion in <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalNY1_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">High tech</a> industries including <a href="/wiki/Digital_media" title="Digital media">digital media</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Game_design" title="Game design">game design</a>, and other fields in <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> are growing, bolstered by New York City's position at the terminus of several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transatlantic_telephone_cable" title="Transatlantic telephone cable">transatlantic fiber optic trunk lines</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_capital" title="Intellectual capital">intellectual capital</a>, as well as its growing outdoor <a href="/wiki/Wireless_network" title="Wireless network">wireless connectivity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> In December 2014, New York State announced a $50 million venture-capital fund to encourage enterprises working in biotechnology and <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">advanced materials</a>; according to Governor Andrew Cuomo, the <a href="/wiki/Seed_money" title="Seed money">seed money</a> would facilitate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entrepreneur" title="Entrepreneur">entrepreneurs</a> in bringing their research into the marketplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> On December 19, 2011, then Mayor Michael R. Bloomberg announced his choice of <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technion-Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion-Israel Institute of Technology">Technion-Israel Institute of Technology</a> to build a US$2 billion <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate school</a> of <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied sciences</a> on <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island" title="Roosevelt Island">Roosevelt Island</a> in Manhattan, with the goal of transforming New York City into the world's premier technology capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tech_Valley">Tech Valley</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tech_Valley" title="Tech Valley">Tech Valley</a></div>
<p>Albany,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeInAlbanyNY_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-MadeInAlbanyNY-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_County,_New_York" title="Saratoga County, New York">Saratoga County</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeInSaratogaCountyNY_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-MadeInSaratogaCountyNY-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_County,_New_York" title="Rensselaer County, New York">Rensselaer County</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a>, collectively recognized as eastern New York's <a href="/wiki/Tech_Valley" title="Tech Valley">Tech Valley</a>, have experienced significant growth in the <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">computer hardware</a> side of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-technology_industry" title="High-technology industry">high-technology industry</a>, with great strides in the <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a> sector, <a href="/wiki/Digital_electronics" title="Digital electronics">digital electronics</a> design, and water- and electricity-dependent <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated microchip circuit</a> manufacturing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeInSaratogaCountyNY_176-1"><a href="#cite_note-MadeInSaratogaCountyNY-176">[176]</a></sup> involving companies including <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Watson_Research_Center" title="Thomas J. Watson Research Center">Thomas J. Watson Research Center</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GlobalFoundries" title="GlobalFoundries">GlobalFoundries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_Semiconductor" title="Taiwan Semiconductor">Taiwan Semiconductor</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeInAlbanyNY_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-MadeInAlbanyNY-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> The area's high technology ecosystem is supported by technologically focused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia" title="Academia">academic institutions</a> including <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_Polytechnic_Institute" title="State University of New York Polytechnic Institute">SUNY Polytechnic Institute</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MadeInAlbanyNY_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-MadeInAlbanyNY-175">[175]</a></sup> In 2015, Tech Valley, straddling both sides of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adirondack_Northway" title="Adirondack Northway">Adirondack Northway</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Thruway" title="New York Thruway">New York Thruway</a>, generated over US$163 million in venture capital investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalNY1_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester</a> area is important in the field of <a href="/wiki/Photographic_processing" title="Photographic processing">photographic processing and imaging</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">incubating</a> an increasingly diverse high technology sphere encompassing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/STEM_fields" title="STEM fields">STEM fields</a>, similarly in part the result of private <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startup enterprises</a> collaborating with major academic institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Rochester" title="University of Rochester">University of Rochester</a> and Cornell University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">Westchester County</a> has developed a burgeoning <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology sector</a> in the 21st century, with over US$1 billion in planned private investment as of 2016,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_entertainment">Media and entertainment</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_New_York_City" title="Media in New York City">Media in New York City</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">Creative industries</a>, which are concerned with generating and distributing <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a>, such as new media, digital media, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_production" title="Film production">film</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_production" title="Television production">television production</a>, advertising, fashion, design, and architecture, account for a growing share of employment, with New York City possessing a strong competitive advantage in these industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, New York State was offering tax incentives of up to $420 million annually for <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">filmmaking</a> within the state, the most generous such <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_rebate" title="Tax rebate">tax rebate</a> among the U.S. states. New York has also attracted higher-wage <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual-effects</a> employment by further augmenting its tax credit to a maximum of 35% for performing <a href="/wiki/Post-production" title="Post-production">post-film production</a> work in Upstate New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> The filmed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entertainment_industry" title="Entertainment industry">entertainment industry</a> has been growing in New York, contributing nearly US$9 billion to the New York City economy alone as of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I_Love_New_York.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="279" data-file-width="300" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I_Love_New_York.svg/220px-I_Love_New_York.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I_Love_New_York.svg/330px-I_Love_New_York.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/I_Love_New_York.svg/440px-I_Love_New_York.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:I_Love_New_York.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/I_Love_New_York" title="I Love New York">I Love New York</a></i> logo has been used by the state since 1977.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_New_York_City" title="Tourism in New York City">Tourism in New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls" title="Niagara Falls">Niagara Falls</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway theatre</a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/I_Love_New_York" title="I Love New York">I Love New York</a></i> (stylized <i>I ❤ NY</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Logo" title="Logo">logo</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Song" title="Song">song</a> that are the basis of an <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a> campaign and has been used since 1977 to promote <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> in the state of New York,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trademarked" title="Trademarked">trademarked</a> logo is owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State_Empire_State_Development" title="New York State Empire State Development">New York State Empire State Development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Broadway_League" title="The Broadway League">The Broadway League</a> reported that Broadway shows sold approximately US$1.27 billion worth of tickets in the 2013–2014 season, an 11.4% increase from US$1.139 billion in the 2012–2013 season. Attendance in 2013–2014 stood at 12.21 million, representing a 5.5% increase from the 2012–2013 season's 11.57 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-league_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-league-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>I Love New York</i> song is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_song" title="State song">state song</a> of New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exports">Exports</span></h3>
<p>New York exports a wide variety of goods such as prepared foods, <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">electronics</a>, cut <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, and other commodities. In 2007, the state exported a total of $71.1 billion worth of goods, with the five largest foreign export markets being <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (US$15 billion), the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (US$6 billion), <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (US$5.9 billion), <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> (US$4.9 billion), and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> (US$3.4 billion). New York's largest imports are oil, gold, aluminum, natural gas, electricity, rough diamonds, and lumber. The state also has a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manufacturing_sector" title="Manufacturing sector">manufacturing sector</a> that includes printing and the production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garment" title="Garment">garments</a>, mainly in New York City; and furs, railroad equipment, automobile parts, and bus line vehicles, concentrated in Upstate regions.</p>
<p>New York is the nation's third-largest <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grape</a> producing state, and second-largest <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> producer by volume, behind California. The southern <a href="/wiki/Finger_Lakes" title="Finger Lakes">Finger Lakes</a> hillsides, the Hudson Valley, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Fork,_Suffolk_County,_New_York" title="North Fork, Suffolk County, New York">North Fork</a> of Long Island, and the southern shore of Lake Erie are the primary grape- and wine-growing regions in New York, with many <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a>. In 2012, New York had 320 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wineries" title="Wineries">wineries</a> and 37,000 grape bearing acres, generating full-time employment of nearly 25,000 and annual wages of over US$1.1 billion, and yielding US$4.8 billion in direct economic impact from New York grapes, grape juice, and wine and grape products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>New York is a major agricultural producer overall, ranking among the top five states for agricultural products including <a href="/wiki/Maple_syrup" title="Maple syrup">maple syrup</a>, apples, cherries, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, dairy products, onions, and potatoes. The state is the largest producer of cabbage in the U.S. The state has about a quarter of its land in farms and produced $3.4 billion in agricultural products in 2001. The south shore of Lake Ontario provides the right mix of <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">soils</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimate</a> for many apple, cherry, <a href="/wiki/Plum" title="Plum">plum</a>, pear and <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peach</a> <a href="/wiki/Orchard" title="Orchard">orchards</a>. Apples are also grown in the Hudson Valley and near Lake Champlain. A moderately sized saltwater <a href="/wiki/Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">commercial fishery</a> is located along the Atlantic side of Long Island. The principal catches by value are clams, lobsters, squid, and <a href="/wiki/Flounder" title="Flounder">flounder</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_New_York_(state)" title="Education in New York (state)">Education in New York (state)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime,_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3096" data-file-width="3960" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg/220px-New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg/330px-New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg/440px-New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_York_State_of_Education_building_daytime,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Education_Department_Building" title="New York State Education Department Building">New York State Education Department Building</a>, Albany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_State_of_New_York" title="University of the State of New York">University of the State of New York</a> accredits and sets standards for primary, middle-level, and secondary education in the state, while the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Education_Department" title="New York State Education Department">New York State Education Department</a> oversees public schools and controls their <a href="/wiki/Standardized_test" title="Standardized test">standardized tests</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">New York City Department of Education</a> manages the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_Public_Schools" title="New York City Public Schools">New York City Public Schools</a> system. In 1894, reflecting general racial discrimination then, the state passed a law that allowed communities to set up separate schools for children of African-American descent. In 1900, the state passed another law requiring integrated schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the level of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_United_States" title="Higher education in the United States">post-secondary education</a>, the statewide public university system is the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">State University of New York</a>, commonly referred to as SUNY. New York City also has its own <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">City University of New York</a> system, which is funded by the city. The SUNY system consists of 64 community colleges, technical colleges, undergraduate colleges, and doctoral-granting institutions, including several universities. New York's largest public university is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Buffalo" title="State University of New York at Buffalo">State University of New York at Buffalo</a>, which was founded by U.S President and Vice President <a href="/wiki/Millard_Fillmore" title="Millard Fillmore">Millard Fillmore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> The four SUNY University Centers, offering a wide array of academic programs, are the <a href="/wiki/University_at_Albany,_SUNY" title="University at Albany, SUNY">University at Albany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Binghamton_University" title="Binghamton University">Binghamton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_University" title="Stony Brook University">Stony Brook University</a>, and the University at Buffalo.</p>
<p>Notable large private universities include the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Manhattan" title="Upper Manhattan">Upper Manhattan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> institutions, as well as <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fordham_University" title="Fordham University">Fordham University</a> in the Bronx, Manhattan, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westchester_County" title="Westchester County">Westchester County</a>. Smaller notable private institutions of higher education include <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">Rockefeller University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercy_College_(New_York)" title="Mercy College (New York)">Mercy College</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Institute_of_Technology" title="New York Institute of Technology">New York Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva_University" title="Yeshiva University">Yeshiva University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hofstra_University" title="Hofstra University">Hofstra University</a>. There are also a multitude of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postgraduate_degree" title="Postgraduate degree">postgraduate</a>-level schools in New York State, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_School" title="Medical School">Medical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_School" title="Law School">Law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">Engineering</a> schools. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">West Point</a>, the service academy of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a>, is located just south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newburgh_(city),_New_York" title="Newburgh (city), New York">Newburgh</a>, on the west bank of the Hudson River.</p>
<p>During the fiscal 2013 year, New York spent more on public education per pupil than any other state, according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a> statistics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_York" title="Transportation in New York">Transportation in New York</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG/220px-TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG/330px-TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG/440px-TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TappanZeeBridgeFromBelow.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Tappan_Zee_Bridge" title="Tappan Zee Bridge">Tappan Zee Bridge</a>, linking <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">Westchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rockland_County,_New_York" title="Rockland County, New York">Rockland</a> counties, is the second-longest bridge in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">northeastern United States</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg"><img alt="Five jumbo airplanes wait in a line on a runway next to a small body of water. Behind them in the distance is the airport and control tower." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2414" data-file-width="3620" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg/220px-JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg/330px-JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg/440px-JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JFK_Plane_Queue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy Airport</a> in Queens, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_States_by_international_passenger_traffic" title="Busiest airports in the United States by international passenger traffic">busiest international air passenger gateway</a> to the United States.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:R46_Subway_Car,_5732,_F,_September_5th,_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="2700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg/220px-R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg/330px-R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg/440px-R46_Subway_Car%2C_5732%2C_F%2C_September_5th%2C_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:R46_Subway_Car,_5732,_F,_September_5th,_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> is <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">one of the world's busiest</a>, serving a passenger ridership of over 5 million per average weekday.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>New York has one of the most extensive and one of the oldest transportation infrastructures in the country. Engineering challenges posed by the complex terrain of the state and the unique infrastructural issues of New York City brought on by urban crowding have had to be overcome perennially. Population expansion of the state has followed the path of the early waterways, first the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk River</a>, then the <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie Canal</a>. In the 19th century, railroads were constructed along the river valleys, followed by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Thruway" title="New York State Thruway">New York State Thruway</a> in the 20th century.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Department_of_Transportation" title="New York State Department of Transportation">New York State Department of Transportation</a> (NYSDOT) is the department of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_(state)" title="Government of New York (state)">government of New York</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> responsible for the development and operation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highways" title="Highways">highways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">railroads</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_transit" title="Mass transit">mass transit</a> systems, <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterways" title="Waterways">waterways</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a> facilities within New York State. The NYSDOT is headquartered at 50 Wolf Road in <a href="/wiki/Colonie,_New_York" title="Colonie, New York">Colonie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albany_County,_New_York" title="Albany County, New York">Albany County</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port Authority of New York and New Jersey">Port Authority of New York and New Jersey</a> (PANYNJ) is a joint venture between the States of New York and New Jersey and authorized by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Congress" title="US Congress">US Congress</a>, established in 1921 through an <a href="/wiki/Interstate_compact" title="Interstate compact">interstate compact</a>, that oversees much of the regional transportation infrastructure, including <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">bridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunnel" title="Tunnel">tunnels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airport" title="Airport">airports</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">seaports</a>, within the geographical jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey" title="Port of New York and New Jersey">Port of New York and New Jersey</a>. This 1,500 square mile (3,900 km²) port district is generally encompassed within a 25-mile (40 km) radius of the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty_National_Monument" title="Statue of Liberty National Monument">Statue of Liberty National Monument</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PANYNJ-annual-report-2002_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-PANYNJ-annual-report-2002-197">[197]</a></sup> The Port Authority is headquartered at <a href="/wiki/4_World_Trade_Center" title="4 World Trade Center">4 World Trade Center</a> in Lower Manhattan.</p>
<p>In addition to the well known <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a> system – which is confined within New York City – four suburban <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commuter_railroad" title="Commuter railroad">commuter railroad</a> systems enter and leave the city: the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">Long Island Rail Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North Railroad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Trans-Hudson" title="Port Authority Trans-Hudson">Port Authority Trans-Hudson</a>, and five of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Transit_Rail_Operations" title="New Jersey Transit Rail Operations">New Jersey Transit's rail lines</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Transportation" title="New York City Department of Transportation">New York City Department of Transportation</a> (NYCDOT) is the agency of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_City" title="Government of New York City">government of New York City</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> responsible for the management of much of New York City's own transportation infrastructure. Other cities and towns in New York have urban and regional public transportation. In Buffalo, the <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Frontier_Transportation_Authority" title="Niagara Frontier Transportation Authority">Niagara Frontier Transportation Authority</a> runs the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Metro_Rail" title="Buffalo Metro Rail">Buffalo Metro Rail</a> light-rail system; in Rochester, the <a href="/wiki/Rochester_Subway" title="Rochester Subway">Rochester Subway</a> operated from 1927 until 1956, but fell into disuse as state and federal investment went to highways.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Department_of_Motor_Vehicles" title="New York State Department of Motor Vehicles">New York State Department of Motor Vehicles</a> (NYSDMV or DMV) is the governmental agency responsible for registering and <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_inspection" title="Vehicle inspection">inspecting automobiles</a> and other motor vehicles, as well as licensing drivers in the State of New York. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_(state)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the NYSDMV has 11,284,546 drivers licenses on file<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> and 10,697,644 vehicle registrations in force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> All gasoline-powered vehicles registered in New York State are required to have an <a href="/wiki/Emission_standard" title="Emission standard">emissions inspection</a> every 12 months, in order to ensure that <a href="/wiki/Environmental_quality" title="Environmental quality">environmental quality</a> controls are working to prevent air pollution. Diesel-powered vehicles with a gross weight rating over 8,500 lb that are registered in most Downstate New York counties must get an annual emissions inspection. All vehicles registered in New York State must get an annual safety inspection.</p>
<p>Portions of the transportation system are <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_passenger_transport" title="Intermodal passenger transport">intermodal</a>, allowing travelers to switch easily from one mode of transportation to another. One of the most notable examples is <a href="/wiki/AirTrain_JFK" title="AirTrain JFK">AirTrain JFK</a> which allows rail passengers to travel directly to <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminals</a> at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> as well as to the underground New York City Subway system.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2825" data-file-width="4758" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg/220px-NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg/330px-NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg/440px-NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NYSCapitolPanorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Capitol" title="New York State Capitol">New York State Capitol</a> in Albany</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_(state)" title="Government of New York (state)">Government of New York (state)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1007" data-file-width="723" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg/170px-Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg/255px-Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg/340px-Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Cuomo_by_Pat_Arnow_cropped.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cuomo" title="Andrew Cuomo">Andrew Cuomo</a> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">(D)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_New_York" title="List of Governors of New York">56th</a> and current <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Government of New York embodies the governmental structure of the State of New York as established by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State_Constitution" title="New York State Constitution">New York State Constitution</a>. It is composed of three branches: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_branch" title="Executive branch">executive</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" title="Legislative branch">legislative</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" title="Judicial branch">judicial</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor</a> is the State's chief executive and is assisted by the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_New_York" title="Lieutenant Governor of New York">Lieutenant Governor</a>. Both are elected on the same ticket. Additional elected officers include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Attorney_General" title="New York Attorney General">Attorney General</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Comptroller" title="New York State Comptroller">Comptroller</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_New_York" title="Secretary of State of New York">Secretary of State</a>, formerly an elected officer, is currently appointed by the Governor.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Legislature" title="New York State Legislature">New York State Legislature</a> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> and consists of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Senate" title="New York State Senate">New York State Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Assembly" title="New York State Assembly">New York State Assembly</a>. The Assembly consists of 150 members, while the Senate varies in its number of members, currently having 63. The Legislature is empowered to make laws, subject to the Governor's power to <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> a bill. However, the veto may be overridden by the Legislature if there is a <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">two-thirds majority</a> in favor of overriding in each House. The permanent laws of a general nature are <a href="/wiki/Codification_(law)" title="Codification (law)">codified</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Consolidated_Laws_of_New_York" title="Consolidated Laws of New York">Consolidated Laws of New York</a></i>.</p>
<p>The highest court of appeal in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_New_York" title="Judiciary of New York">Unified Court System</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State_Court_of_Appeals" title="New York State Court of Appeals">Court of Appeals</a> whereas the primary <a href="/wiki/Felony" title="Felony">felony</a> <a href="/wiki/Trial_court" title="Trial court">trial court</a> is the <a href="/wiki/New_York_County_Court" title="New York County Court">County Court</a> (or the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Supreme_Court" title="New York Supreme Court">Supreme Court</a> in New York City). The Supreme Court also acts as the intermediate appellate court for many cases, and the local courts handle a variety of other matters including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_claims" title="Small claims">small claims</a>, traffic ticket cases, and local <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">zoning</a> matters, and are the starting point for all criminal cases. The <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_courts" title="New York City courts">New York City courts</a> make up the largest local court system.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_New_York" title="Administrative divisions of New York">state is divided</a> into counties, cities, towns, and villages, all of which are <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">municipal corporations</a> with respect to their own governments, as well as various corporate entities that serve single purposes that are also local governments, such as school districts, fire districts, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_state_public-benefit_corporations" title="New York state public-benefit corporations">New York state public-benefit corporations</a>, frequently known as <i>authorities</i> or <i>development corporations</i>. Each municipal corporation is granted varying <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> powers as provided by the New York Constitution. The state also has 10 <a href="/wiki/Indian_reservation" title="Indian reservation">Indian reservations</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_punishment">Capital punishment</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_New_York" title="Capital punishment in New York">Capital punishment in New York</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_United_States" title="Capital punishment in the United States">Capital punishment</a> was reintroduced in 1995 under the <a href="/wiki/George_Pataki#Death_penalty" title="George Pataki">Pataki administration</a>, but the statute was declared unconstitutional in 2004, when the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Court_of_Appeals" title="New York Court of Appeals">New York Court of Appeals</a> ruled in <i><a href="/wiki/People_v._LaValle" title="People v. LaValle">People v. LaValle</a></i> that it violated the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Constitution" title="New York Constitution">state constitution</a>. The remaining death sentence was commuted by the court to <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment" title="Life imprisonment">life imprisonment</a> in 2007, in <i>People v. John Taylor</i>, and the death row was disestablished in 2008, under executive order from <a href="/wiki/David_Paterson" title="David Paterson">Governor Paterson</a>. No execution has taken place in New York since 1963. Legislative efforts to amend the statute have failed, and death sentences are no longer sought at the state level, though certain crimes that fall under the jurisdiction of the federal government are subject to the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_by_the_United_States_federal_government" title="Capital punishment by the United States federal government">federal death penalty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_representation">Federal representation</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_delegations_from_New_York#2013.E2.80.932023:_27_seats" title="United States congressional delegations from New York">Current United States congressional delegation from New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_congressional_districts" title="New York's congressional districts">New York's congressional districts</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2297" data-file-width="1780" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Chuck_Schumer_official_photo_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Schumer" title="Charles Schumer">Charles Schumer</a> (D), New York's current senior <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senator" title="U.S. Senator">U.S. Senator</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kirsten_Gillibrand,_official_portrait,_112th_Congress.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2368" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg/150px-Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg/225px-Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg/300px-Kirsten_Gillibrand%2C_official_portrait%2C_112th_Congress.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Gillibrand" title="Kirsten Gillibrand">Kirsten Gillibrand</a> (D), New York's current junior U.S. Senator</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg/170px-The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg/255px-The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg/340px-The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_United_Nations_Secretariat_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">United Nations Headquarters</a> has been situated on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midtown_East" title="Midtown East">East Side of Midtown Manhattan</a> since 1952.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The State of New York sends <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_congressional_districts" title="New York's congressional districts">27</a> members to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> in addition to its two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" title="United States Senator">United States Senators</a>. As of the 2000 census and the redistricting for the 2002 elections, the state had 29 members in the House, but the representation was reduced to 27 in 2013 due to the state's slower overall population growth relative to the overall national population growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reybn_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-reybn-205">[205]</a></sup> From 2016, New York will have 29 <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> in national presidential elections (a drop from its peak of 47 votes from 1933 to 1953).</p>
<p>New York is represented by <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Schumer" title="Chuck Schumer">Chuck Schumer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Gillibrand" title="Kirsten Gillibrand">Kirsten Gillibrand</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> and has the nation's third equal highest number of congressional districts, equal with Florida and behind California's 53 and Texas's 36.</p>
<p>The state has a strong imbalance of payments with the federal government. According to the Office of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Comptroller" title="New York State Comptroller">New York State Comptroller</a>, New York State received 91 cents in services for every $1 it sent in taxes to the U.S. federal government in the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a>; New York ranked in 46th place in the federal balance of payments to the state on a per capita basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York,_2016.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3201" data-file-width="2904" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg/300px-United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg/450px-United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg/600px-United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_New_York,_2016.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treemap" title="Treemap">Treemap</a> of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_New_York" title="Elections in New York">Elections in New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_New_York" title="Political party strength in New York">Political party strength in New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_New_York_(state)" title="Politics of New York (state)">Politics of New York (state)</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_of_New_York" title="Law of New York">Law of New York</a></div>
<p>As of April 2016, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> represented a plurality of voters in New York State, constituting over twice as many <a href="/wiki/Voter_registration" title="Voter registration">registered voters</a> as any other political party affiliation <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">or lack thereof</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSRegisteredVoterAffiliation_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYSRegisteredVoterAffiliation-207">[207]</a></sup> Since the second half of the 20th century, New York has generally supported candidates belonging to the Democratic Party in national elections. Democratic presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> won New York State by over 25 percentage points in both 2012 and 2008. New York City, as well as the state's other major urban locales, including Albany, Buffalo, Rochester, Yonkers, and Syracuse, are significant Democratic strongholds, with <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberal politics</a>. Rural portions of upstate New York, however, are generally more conservative than the cities and tend to favor <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a>. Heavily populated suburban areas downstate, such as Westchester County and Long Island, have swung between the major parties since the 1980s, but more often than not support Democrats.</p>
<p>New York City is the most important source of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_fundraising" title="Political fundraising">political fundraising</a> in the United States for both major parties. Four of the top five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zip_code" title="Zip code">zip codes</a> in the nation for political contributions are in Manhattan. The top zip code, 10021 on the <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a>, generated the most money for the 2000 presidential campaigns of both <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state of New York has the distinction of being the home state for both major-party nominees in three <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">Presidential elections</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1904" title="United States presidential election, 1904">1904 presidential election</a> saw former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Governor" title="New York Governor">New York Governor</a> and incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> face <a href="/wiki/Alton_B._Parker" title="Alton B. Parker">Alton B. Parker</a>, chief judge of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Court_of_Appeals" title="New York Court of Appeals">New York Court of Appeals</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1944" title="United States presidential election, 1944">1944 presidential election</a> had <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, following in his cousin Theodore's footsteps as former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Governor" title="New York Governor">New York Governor</a> and incumbent president running for re-election against then-current New York Governor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey" title="Thomas E. Dewey">Thomas E. Dewey</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016 Presidential election</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" title="United States Senator">United States Senator</a> from New York <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>, a resident of <a href="/wiki/Chappaqua,_New_York" title="Chappaqua, New York">Chappaqua</a>, was the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> nominee. The <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> nominee was businessman <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, a resident of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> and a native of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>New York City is an important center for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_diplomacy" title="International diplomacy">international diplomacy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">United Nations Headquarters</a> has been situated on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midtown_East" title="Midtown East">East Side of Midtown Manhattan</a> since 1952.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2067" data-file-width="2991" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg/220px-Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg/330px-Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg/440px-Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_2009_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperstown" title="Cooperstown">Cooperstown</a> draws about 300,000 visitors each year.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Belmont8_1999-05.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1544" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Belmont8_1999-05.jpg/190px-Belmont8_1999-05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Belmont8_1999-05.jpg/285px-Belmont8_1999-05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Belmont8_1999-05.jpg/380px-Belmont8_1999-05.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Belmont_Park" title="Belmont Park">Belmont Park</a> on Long Island hosts the <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Stakes" title="Belmont Stakes">Belmont Stakes</a>, part of the horse racing <a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_of_Thoroughbred_Racing_(United_States)" title="Triple Crown of Thoroughbred Racing (United States)">Triple Crown</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg/190px-National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg/285px-National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg/380px-National_Museum_of_Racing.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Racing_and_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Museum of Racing and Hall of Fame">National Museum of Racing and Hall of Fame</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_Springs,_New_York" title="Saratoga Springs, New York">Saratoga Springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_County,_New_York" title="Saratoga County, New York">Saratoga County</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Champlain.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4290" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lake_Champlain.jpg/220px-Lake_Champlain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lake_Champlain.jpg/330px-Lake_Champlain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Lake_Champlain.jpg/440px-Lake_Champlain.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Champlain.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lake_Champlain" title="Lake Champlain">Lake Champlain</a>, at the base of the Adirondack Mountains, is popular with nature observers as well as water sportsmen.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_New_York" title="Sports in New York">Sports in New York</a></div>
<p>New York State is geographically home to one <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> team, the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a>, based in the Buffalo suburb of <a href="/wiki/Orchard_Park_(town),_New_York" title="Orchard Park (town), New York">Orchard Park</a>. Although the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> represent the <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a> and were previously located in New York City, they play in <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a>. New York also has two <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> teams, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> (based in <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> (based in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>). Minor league baseball teams also play in the State of New York, including the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Ducks" title="Long Island Ducks">Long Island Ducks</a>. New York is home to three <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> franchises: the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">New York Rangers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Islanders" title="New York Islanders">New York Islanders</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Sabres" title="Buffalo Sabres">Buffalo Sabres</a> in Buffalo. New York has two <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> teams, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> in Manhattan, and the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a> in Brooklyn. New York is the home of a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> franchise, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_FC" title="New York City FC">New York City FC</a>, currently playing in the Bronx. Although the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> represent the New York metropolitan area, they play in <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Arena_(New_Jersey)" title="Red Bull Arena (New Jersey)">Red Bull Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_Jersey" title="Harrison, New Jersey">Harrison, New Jersey</a>.</p>
<p>New York hosted the <a href="/wiki/1932_Winter_Olympics" title="1932 Winter Olympics">1932</a> and <a href="/wiki/1980_Winter_Olympics" title="1980 Winter Olympics">1980 Winter Olympics</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Placid,_New_York" title="Lake Placid, New York">Lake Placid</a>. The 1980 Games are known for the USA–USSR <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> match dubbed the "<a href="/wiki/Miracle_on_Ice" title="Miracle on Ice">Miracle on Ice</a>", in which a group of American college students and amateurs defeated the heavily favored Soviet national ice hockey team 4–3 and went on to win the gold medal against <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>. Along with <a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">Innsbruck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, Lake Placid is one of the three cities to have hosted the Winter Olympic Games twice. New York City <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_bid_for_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="New York City bid for the 2012 Summer Olympics">bid</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> but lost to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.</p>
<p>Several U.S. national sports halls of fame are or have been situated in New York. The <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum</a> is located in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperstown" title="Cooperstown">Cooperstown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otsego_County,_New_York" title="Otsego County, New York">Otsego County</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Racing_and_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Museum of Racing and Hall of Fame">National Museum of Racing and Hall of Fame</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_Springs,_New_York" title="Saratoga Springs, New York">Saratoga Springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saratoga_County,_New_York" title="Saratoga County, New York">Saratoga County</a>, honors achievements in the sport of <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">thoroughbred horse racing</a>. The physical facility of the <a href="/wiki/National_Soccer_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Soccer Hall of Fame">National Soccer Hall of Fame</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oneonta,_New_York" title="Oneonta, New York">Oneonta</a>, also in Otsego County, closed in 2010, although the organization itself has continued inductions. The annual <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">United States Open Tennis Championships</a> is one of the world's four <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tennis tournaments and is held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USTA_National_Tennis_Center" title="USTA National Tennis Center">National Tennis Center</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flushing_Meadows-Corona_Park" title="Flushing Meadows-Corona Park">Flushing Meadows-Corona Park</a> in the New York City borough of Queens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
